\hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm}{}\doxysection{phreeqcrm Module Reference}
\label{namespacephreeqcrm}\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}


Fortran Documentation for the geochemical reaction module Phreeqc\+RM.  


\doxysubsection*{Functions/\+Subroutines}
\begin{DoxyCompactItemize}
\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ae8a50594bacfaf961614749f94ce16d2}{rm\+\_\+abort}} (id, irm\+\_\+result, err\+\_\+str)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Abort the program. {\itshape irm\+\_\+result} will be interpreted as an I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT value and decoded; {\itshape err\+\_\+str} will be printed; and the reaction module will be destroyed. If using M\+PI, an M\+P\+I\+\_\+\+Abort message will be sent before the reaction module is destroyed. If the {\itshape id} is an invalid instance, R\+M\+\_\+\+Abort will return a value of I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+B\+A\+D\+I\+N\+S\+T\+A\+N\+CE, otherwise the program will exit with a return code of 4. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a83e657f568c90b0cdfcbc5f0b6773744}{rm\+\_\+closefiles}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Close the output and log files. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_afd0d3fa630c28207e4243323e04e56df}{rm\+\_\+concentrations2utility}} (id, c, n, tc, p\+\_\+atm)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em {\itshape N} sets of component concentrations are converted to S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+Ns numbered 1-\/{\itshape n} in the Utility I\+Phreeqc. The solutions can be reacted and manipulated with the methods of I\+Phreeqc. If solution concentration units (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution) are per liter, one liter of solution is created in the Utility instance; if solution concentration units are mass fraction, one kilogram of solution is created in the Utility instance. The motivation for this method is the mixing of solutions in wells, where it may be necessary to calculate solution properties (pH for example) or react the mixture to form scale minerals. The code fragments below make a mixture of concentrations and then calculate the pH of the mixture. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a8b7992170b1f1d5cd884a42e3197af7f}{rm\+\_\+create}} (nxyz, nthreads)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Creates a reaction module. If the code is compiled with the preprocessor directive U\+S\+E\+\_\+\+O\+P\+E\+N\+MP, the reaction module is multithreaded. If the code is compiled with the preprocessor directive U\+S\+E\+\_\+\+M\+PI, the reaction module will use M\+PI and multiple processes. If neither preprocessor directive is used, the reaction module will be serial (unparallelized). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a6f84c89597ef9e7c076d52aeadbbec07}{rm\+\_\+createmapping}} (id, grid2chem)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Provides a mapping from grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model to reaction cells in Phreeqc\+RM. The mapping is used to eliminate inactive cells and to use symmetry to decrease the number of cells for which chemistry must be run. The array {\itshape grid2chem} of size {\itshape nxyz} (the number of grid cells, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count) must contain the set of all integers 0 $<$= {\itshape i} $<$ {\itshape count\+\_\+chemistry}, where {\itshape count\+\_\+chemistry} is a number less than or equal to {\itshape nxyz}. Inactive cells are assigned a negative integer. The mapping may be many-\/to-\/one to account for symmetry. Default is a one-\/to-\/one mapping--all user grid cells are reaction cells (equivalent to {\itshape grid2chem} values of 0,1,2,3,...,{\itshape nxyz-\/1}). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a19846f60cecda1fa4638e43962c1fed9}{rm\+\_\+decodeerror}} (id, e)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em If {\itshape e} is negative, this method prints an error message corresponding to I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT {\itshape e}. If {\itshape e} is non-\/negative, no action is taken. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aa18cd6cf17f8ac7b5552880340d5a3d2}{rm\+\_\+destroy}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Destroys a reaction module. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a0f9f244f6dc110b82ac2afe4da816352}{rm\+\_\+dumpmodule}} (id, dump\+\_\+on, append)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Writes the contents of all workers to file in \+\_\+\+R\+AW formats, including S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+Ns and all reactants. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a73c704101dd8f52b2555ba84322a3b69}{rm\+\_\+errormessage}} (id, errstr)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Send an error message to the screen, the output file, and the log file. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a6553114482cfbf520b545a4f67dcf716}{rm\+\_\+findcomponents}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of items in the list of all elements in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. Elements are those that have been defined in a solution or any other reactant (E\+Q\+U\+I\+L\+I\+B\+R\+I\+U\+M\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE, K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS, and others). The method can be called multiple times and the list that is created is cummulative. The list is the set of components that needs to be transported. By default the list includes water, excess H and excess O (the H and O not contained in water); alternatively, the list may be set to contain total H and total O (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Component\+H2O), which requires transport results to be accurate to eight or nine significant digits. If multicomponent diffusion (M\+CD) is to be modeled, there is a capability to retrieve aqueous species concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations) and to set new solution concentrations after M\+CD by using individual species concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module). To use these methods the save-\/species property needs to be turned on (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On). If the save-\/species property is on, R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components will generate a list of aqueous species (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Name), their diffusion coefficients at 25 C (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+D25), their charge (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+SpeciesZ). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a3ff0a071b0d5a887ac3c2eb975c51865}{rm\+\_\+getbackwardmapping}} (id, n, list, size)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Fills an array with the cell numbers in the user\textquotesingle{}s numbering sytstem that map to a cell in the Phreeqc\+RM numbering system. The mapping is defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Create\+Mapping. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a8d94a837de9e65cdafab4c783027ee4d}{rm\+\_\+getchemistrycellcount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of chemistry cells in the reaction module. The number of chemistry cells is defined by the set of non-\/negative integers in the mapping from user grid cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Create\+Mapping). The number of chemistry cells is less than or equal to the number of cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a315d001eefce7c311fe237a6aafe15c6}{rm\+\_\+getcomponent}} (id, num, comp\+\_\+name)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Retrieves an item from the reaction-\/module component list that was generated by calls to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aba238e639d401d1d3ff9891d2fc6d665}{rm\+\_\+getcomponentcount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of components in the reaction-\/module component list. The component list is generated by calls to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components. The return value from the last call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components is equal to the return value from R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a89e51efde75f2daf0a1195029417f33c}{rm\+\_\+getconcentrations}} (id, c)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Transfer solution concentrations from each reaction cell to the concentration array given in the argument list ({\itshape c}). Units of concentration for {\itshape c} are defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution. For concentration units of per liter, the solution volume is used to calculate the concentrations for {\itshape c}. For mass fraction concentration units, the solution mass is used to calculate concentrations for {\itshape c}. Two options are available for the volume and mass of solution that are used in converting to transport concentrations\+: (1) the volume and mass of solution are calculated by P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC, or (2) the volume of solution is the product of saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume), and the mass of solution is volume times density as defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density. R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume determines which option is used. For option 1, the databases that have partial molar volume definitions needed to accurately calculate solution volume are phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a10f9403c1742b94ddcf9e036c0f24d7b}{rm\+\_\+getdensity}} (id, density)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Transfer solution densities from the reaction cells to the array given in the argument list ({\itshape density}). Densities are those calculated by the reaction module. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate density\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a46d1ef91643490ac431a50fc9f45255b}{rm\+\_\+getendcell}} (id, ec)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns an array with the ending cell numbers from the range of cell numbers assigned to each worker. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a51ec607a0123e488a6fb2966c6397124}{rm\+\_\+getequilibriumphasescount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of equilibrium phases in the initial-\/phreeqc module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Equilibrium\+Phases\+Count. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to equilibrium phases. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a41504ff0c14f830fca6484bc789e318d}{rm\+\_\+getequilibriumphasesname}} (id, num, name)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Retrieves an item from the equilibrium phase list. The list includes all phases included in any E\+Q\+U\+I\+L\+I\+B\+R\+I\+U\+M\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+S\+ES definitions in the initial-\/phreeqc module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Equilibrium\+Phases\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to equilibrium phases. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns a string containing error messages related to the last call to a Phreeqc\+RM method to the character argument ({\itshape errstr}). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a5ef4c3183f9571ae469a01361b21c721}{rm\+\_\+getexchangename}} (id, num, name)

The exchange names vector is the same length as the exchange species names vector and provides the corresponding exchange site (for example, X corresponing to NaX). This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to exchangers. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to exchangers. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a0084f395fc749089c80ce0f81a4fe95c}{rm\+\_\+getexchangespeciesname}} (id, num, name)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Retrieves an item from the exchange species list. The list of exchange species (such as \char`\"{}\+Na\+X\char`\"{}) is derived from the list of components (R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components) and the list of all exchange names (such as \char`\"{}\+X\char`\"{}) that are included in E\+X\+C\+H\+A\+N\+GE definitions in the initial-\/phreeqc module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Exchange\+Species\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to exchangers. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Gas\+Components\+Name. Fugacity of a gas component is equal to the pressure of the component times the fugacity coefficient. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the gram formula weights (g/mol) for the components in the reaction-\/module component list. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a03a91cb59130fcee27ae50a9913a0781}{rm\+\_\+getgridcellcount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model, which is defined in the call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. The mapping from grid cells to reaction cells is defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Create\+Mapping. The number of reaction cells may be less than the number of grid cells if there are inactive regions or symmetry in the model definition. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a137485f738772049a34946d7799b6ffc}{rm\+\_\+getiphreeqcid}} (id, i)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns an I\+Phreeqc id for the {\itshape ith} I\+Phreeqc instance in the reaction module. For the threaded version, there are {\itshape nthreads} + 2 I\+Phreeqc instances, where {\itshape nthreads} is defined in the constructor (R\+M\+\_\+\+Create). The number of threads can be determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Thread\+Count. The first {\itshape nthreads} (0 based) instances will be the workers, the next ({\itshape nthreads}) is the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, and the next ({\itshape nthreads} + 1) is the Utility instance. Getting the I\+Phreeqc pointer for one of these instances allows the user to use any of the I\+Phreeqc methods on that instance. For M\+PI, each process has exactly three I\+Phreeqc instances, one worker (number 0), one Initial\+Phreeqc instance (number 1), and one Utility instance (number 2). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a6b3a13f0707d428b7f31d608c8619aea}{rm\+\_\+getkineticreactionscount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of kinetic reactions in the initial-\/phreeqc module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Kinetic\+Reactions\+Count. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to kinetic reactions. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a0e7df976fcb49284d4bd0eacffc7d00e}{rm\+\_\+getkineticreactionsname}} (id, num, name)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Retrieves an item from the kinetic reactions list. The list includes all kinetic reactions included in any K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS definitions in the initial-\/phreeqc module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Kinetic\+Reactions\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to kinetic reactions. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ae04ecbc40c2459af07e1fe156adbd045}{rm\+\_\+getmpimyself}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the M\+PI task number. For the O\+P\+E\+N\+MP version, the task number is always zero and the result of R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Tasks is one. For the M\+PI version, the root task number is zero, and all workers have a task number greater than zero. The number of tasks can be obtained with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Tasks. The number of tasks and computer hosts are determined at run time by the mpiexec command, and the number of reaction-\/module processes is defined by the communicator used in constructing the reaction modules (R\+M\+\_\+\+Create). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aa8592a527010fd499050141a7f771a60}{rm\+\_\+getmpitasks}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of M\+PI processes (tasks) assigned to the reaction module. For the O\+P\+E\+N\+MP version, the number of tasks is always one (although there may be multiple threads, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Thread\+Count), and the task number returned by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself is zero. For the M\+PI version, the number of tasks and computer hosts are determined at run time by the mpiexec command. An M\+PI communicator is used in constructing reaction modules for M\+PI. The communicator may define a subset of the total number of M\+PI processes. The root task number is zero, and all workers have a task number greater than zero. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a648f2f337ef7b2c84a6a43d18aae7ae3}{rm\+\_\+getnthselectedoutputusernumber}} (id, n)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the user number for the {\itshape nth} selected-\/output definition. Definitions are sorted by user number. Phreeqc allows multiple selected-\/output definitions, each of which is assigned a nonnegative integer identifier by the user. The number of definitions can be obtained by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Count. To cycle through all of the definitions, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Nth\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number can be used to identify the user number for each selected-\/output definition in sequence. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number is then used to select that user number for selected-\/output processing. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a9db6b89ad2b650501b612233975e22fe}{rm\+\_\+getsaturation}} (id, sat\+\_\+calc)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns a vector of saturations ({\itshape sat\+\_\+calc}) as calculated by the reaction module. Reactions will change the volume of solution in a cell. The transport code must decide whether to ignore or account for this change in solution volume due to reactions. Following reactions, the cell saturation is calculated as solution volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solution\+Volume) divided by the product of representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume) and the porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity). The cell saturation returned by {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation} may be less than or greater than the saturation set by the transport code (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and may be greater than or less than 1.\+0, even in fully saturated simulations. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate solution volume and saturation\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ad0848d40f094dbaad045b5510c0ad2a1}{rm\+\_\+getselectedoutput}} (id, so)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Populates an array with values from the current selected-\/output definition. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number determines which of the selected-\/output definitions is used to populate the array. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a47ecefc0c413cf4ac1dccc576cbb5426}{rm\+\_\+getselectedoutputcolumncount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of columns in the current selected-\/output definition. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number determines which of the selected-\/output definitions is used. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a65ffdb3279f4e8c09341e154b1b57772}{rm\+\_\+getselectedoutputcount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of selected-\/output definitions. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number determines which of the selected-\/output definitions is used. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a31d6c1e020d7780ae0a456a40570ad0a}{rm\+\_\+getselectedoutputheading}} (id, icol, heading)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns a selected output heading. The number of headings is determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Column\+Count. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number determines which of the selected-\/output definitions is used. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a50d0a1dc69b8ef9399552466d519d577}{rm\+\_\+getselectedoutputrowcount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of rows in the current selected-\/output definition. However, the method is included only for convenience; the number of rows is always equal to the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model, and is equal to R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a39eae2b03e5acf211029e6888d71a124}{rm\+\_\+getsicount}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns the number of phases in the initial-\/phreeqc module for which saturation indices can be calculated. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+S\+I\+Count. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to saturation indices. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a42d09ffd37c53b22f958c168f78e746e}{rm\+\_\+getsiname}} (id, num, name)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Retrieves an item from the list of all phases for which saturation indices can be calculated. The list includes all phases that contain only elements included in the components in the initial-\/phreeqc module. The list assumes that all components are present to be able to calculate the entire list of S\+Is; it may be that one or more components are missing in any specific cell. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+S\+I\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to saturation indices. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns a multiplier to convert time from seconds to another unit, as specified by the user. The reaction module uses seconds as the time unit. The user can set a conversion factor (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Time\+Conversion) and retrieve it with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Time\+Conversion. The reaction module only uses the conversion factor when printing the long version of cell chemistry (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+On), which is rare. integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a767950773edd97935ca81bf9a40694a8}{rm\+\_\+initialphreeqc2concentrations}} (id, bc\+\_\+conc, n\+\_\+boundary, bc1, bc2, f1)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Fills an array ({\itshape bc\+\_\+conc}) with concentrations from solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. The method is used to obtain concentrations for boundary conditions. If a negative value is used for a cell in {\itshape bc1}, then the highest numbered solution in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will be used for that cell. Concentrations may be a mixture of two solutions, {\itshape bc1} and {\itshape bc2}, with a mixing fraction for {\itshape bc1} 1 of {\itshape f1} and mixing fraction for {\itshape bc2} of (1 -\/ {\itshape f1}). A negative value for {\itshape bc2} implies no mixing, and the associated value for {\itshape f1} is ignored. If {\itshape bc2} and {\itshape f1} are omitted, no mixing is used; concentrations are derived from {\itshape bc1} only. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ac3d7e7db76abda97a3d11b3ff1903322}{rm\+\_\+initialphreeqc2module}} (id, ic1, ic2, f1)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Transfer solutions and reactants from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance to the reaction-\/module workers, possibly with mixing. In its simplest form, {\itshape ic1} is used to select initial conditions, including solutions and reactants, for each cell of the model, without mixing. {\itshape ic1} is dimensioned ({\itshape nxyz}, 7), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). The dimension of 7 refers to solutions and reactants in the following order\+: (1) S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+NS, (2) E\+Q\+U\+I\+L\+I\+B\+R\+I\+U\+M\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+S\+ES, (3) E\+X\+C\+H\+A\+N\+GE, (4) S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE, (5) G\+A\+S\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE, (6) S\+O\+L\+I\+D\+\_\+\+S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+NS, and (7) K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS. In Fortran, ic1(100, 4) = 2, indicates that cell 99 (0 based) contains the S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE definition with user number 2 that has been defined in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance (either by R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+File or R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+String). ~\newline
~\newline
 It is also possible to mix solutions and reactants to obtain the initial conditions for cells. For mixing, {\itshape ic2} contains numbers for a second entity that mixes with the entity defined in {\itshape ic1}. {\itshape F1} contains the mixing fraction for {\itshape ic1}, whereas (1 -\/ {\itshape f1}) is the mixing fraction for {\itshape ic2}. In Fortran, ic1(100, 4) = 2, initial\+\_\+conditions2(100, 4) = 3, f1(100, 4) = 0.\+25 indicates that cell 99 (0 based) contains a mixture of 0.\+25 S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE 2 and 0.\+75 S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE 3, where the surface compositions have been defined in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. If the user number in {\itshape ic2} is negative, no mixing occurs. If {\itshape ic2} and {\itshape f1} are omitted, no mixing is used, and initial conditions are derived solely from {\itshape ic1}. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a3a6b64040e8435bd9bbaa871d703a4ba}{rm\+\_\+initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations}} (id, bc\+\_\+conc, n\+\_\+boundary, bc1, bc2, f1)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Fills an array ({\itshape bc\+\_\+conc}) with aqueous species concentrations from solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. The method is used to obtain aqueous species concentrations for boundary conditions. If a negative value is used for a cell in {\itshape bc1}, then the highest numbered solution in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will be used for that cell. Concentrations may be a mixture of two solutions, {\itshape bc1} and {\itshape bc2}, with a mixing fraction for {\itshape bc1} of {\itshape f1} and mixing fraction for {\itshape bc2} of (1 -\/ {\itshape f1}). A negative value for {\itshape bc2} implies no mixing, and the associated value for {\itshape f1} is ignored. If {\itshape bc2} and {\itshape f1} are omitted, no mixing is used; concentrations are derived from {\itshape bc1} only. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aa21e0a61224e6d034dc6d08efe4f5ff1}{rm\+\_\+initialphreeqccell2module}} (id, n\+\_\+user, cell\+\_\+numbers, n\+\_\+cell)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em A cell numbered {\itshape n\+\_\+user} in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance is selected to populate a series of cells. All reactants with the number {\itshape n\+\_\+user} are transferred along with the solution. If M\+IX {\itshape n\+\_\+user} exists, it is used for the definition of the solution. If {\itshape n\+\_\+user} is negative, {\itshape n\+\_\+user} is redefined to be the largest solution or M\+IX number in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. All reactants for each cell in the list {\itshape cell\+\_\+numbers} are removed before the cell definition is copied from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance to the workers. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a7a638bba79ee2f1e0ee82c976507a592}{rm\+\_\+mpiworker}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em M\+PI only. Workers (processes with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself $>$ 0) must call R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker to be able to respond to messages from the root to accept data, perform calculations, and (or) return data. R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker contains a loop that reads a message from root, performs a task, and waits for another message from root. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations, R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations are examples of methods that send a message from root to get the workers to perform a task. The workers will respond to all methods that are designated \char`\"{}workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\char`\"{} in the M\+PI section of the method documentation. The workers will continue to respond to messages from root until root calls R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break. ~\newline
~\newline
 (Advanced) The list of tasks that the workers perform can be extended by using R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback. It is then possible to use the M\+PI processes to perform other developer-\/defined tasks, such as transport calculations, without exiting from the R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker loop. Alternatively, root calls R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break to allow the workers to continue past a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. The workers perform developer-\/defined calculations, and then R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker is called again to respond to requests from root to perform reaction-\/module tasks. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_af1d51a379eeed1c0911ca1dde749e561}{rm\+\_\+mpiworkerbreak}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em M\+PI only. This method is called by root to force workers (processes with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself $>$ 0) to return from a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker contains a loop that reads a message from root, performs a task, and waits for another message from root. The workers respond to all methods that are designated \char`\"{}workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\char`\"{} in the M\+PI section of the method documentation. The workers will continue to respond to messages from root until root calls R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a862d60ba6b11922c2834b4ebca6977dd}{rm\+\_\+openfiles}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Opens the output and log files. Files are named prefix.\+chem.\+txt and prefix.\+log.\+txt based on the prefix defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+File\+Prefix. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_af7aae739781f981c4427344f364e952a}{rm\+\_\+outputmessage}} (id, str)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Print a message to the output file. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a7a50c4b05647d313f1ff16a1b3df379f}{rm\+\_\+runcells}} (id)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Runs a reaction step for all of the cells in the reaction module. Normally, tranport concentrations are transferred to the reaction cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations) before reaction calculations are run. The length of time over which kinetic reactions are integrated is set by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Time\+Step. Other properties that may need to be updated as a result of the transport calculations include porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), temperature (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Temperature), and pressure (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Pressure). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a5163c6455abf6aeff6eee80098fd1718}{rm\+\_\+runfile}} (id, workers, initial\+\_\+phreeqc, utility, chem\+\_\+name)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Run a P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input file. The first three arguments determine which I\+Phreeqc instances will run the file--the workers, the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, and (or) the Utility instance. Input files that modify the thermodynamic database should be run by all three sets of instances. Files with S\+E\+L\+E\+C\+T\+E\+D\+\_\+\+O\+U\+T\+P\+UT definitions that will be used during the time-\/stepping loop need to be run by the workers. Files that contain initial conditions or boundary conditions should be run by the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ae564bbeb02f655cdf8f9ec36f681356c}{rm\+\_\+runstring}} (id, workers, initial\+\_\+phreeqc, utility, input\+\_\+string)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Run a P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input string. The first three arguments determine which I\+Phreeqc instances will run the string--the workers, the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, and (or) the Utility instance. Input strings that modify the thermodynamic database should be run by all three sets of instances. Strings with S\+E\+L\+E\+C\+T\+E\+D\+\_\+\+O\+U\+T\+P\+UT definitions that will be used during the time-\/stepping loop need to be run by the workers. Strings that contain initial conditions or boundary conditions should be run by the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a74b4d681ba480c0391ce449e1f23b48f}{rm\+\_\+screenmessage}} (id, str)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Print message to the screen. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a73b92c2118ef8c81acb35be400e4c422}{rm\+\_\+setcomponenth2o}} (id, tf)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Select whether to include H2O in the component list. The concentrations of H and O must be known accurately (8 to 10 significant digits) for the numerical method of P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC to produce accurate pH and pe values. Because most of the H and O are in the water species, it may be more robust (require less accuracy in transport) to transport the excess H and O (the H and O not in water) and water. The default setting ({\itshape true}) is to include water, excess H, and excess O as components. A setting of {\itshape false} will include total H and total O as components. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Component\+H2O} must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ae8fd22c076ee041c289258d28a904fda}{rm\+\_\+setconcentrations}} (id, c)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Use the vector of concentrations ({\itshape c}) to set the moles of components in each reaction cell. The volume of water in a cell is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and reference volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). The moles of each component are determined by the volume of water and per liter concentrations. If concentration units (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution) are mass fraction, the density (as specified by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density) is used to convert from mass fraction to per mass per liter. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a2f08a3a268c2006b445dfccda018a04b}{rm\+\_\+setconcentrations1d}} (id, c)
\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a9f0208a065e0fa161da2bbf6d2b1aedc}{rm\+\_\+setcurrentselectedoutputusernumber}} (id, n\+\_\+user)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Select the current selected output by user number. The user may define multiple S\+E\+L\+E\+C\+T\+E\+D\+\_\+\+O\+U\+T\+P\+UT data blocks for the workers. A user number is specified for each data block. The value of the argument {\itshape n\+\_\+user} selects which of the S\+E\+L\+E\+C\+T\+E\+D\+\_\+\+O\+U\+T\+P\+UT definitions will be used for selected-\/output operations. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ad888bb4b1ef545b8b3a30c6e851c7538}{rm\+\_\+setdensity}} (id, density)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the density for each reaction cell. These density values are used when converting from transported mass fraction concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution) to produce per liter concentrations during a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations. They are also used when converting from module concentrations to transport concentrations of mass fraction (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations), if R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume is set to {\itshape false}. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the action to be taken when the reaction module encounters an error. Options are 0, return to calling program with an error return code (default); 1, throw an exception, in C++, the exception can be caught, for C and Fortran, the program will exit; or 2, attempt to exit gracefully. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Transfer volumes of gas phases from the array given in the argument list ({\itshape gas\+\_\+volume}) to each reaction cell. The gas-\/phase volume affects the pressures calculated for fixed-\/volume gas phases. If a gas-\/phase volume is defined with this method for a G\+A\+S\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE in a cell, the gas phase is forced to be a fixed-\/volume gas phase. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a9d84a73516473581c605807c48c711c6}{rm\+\_\+setmpiworkercallback}} (id, fcn)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em M\+PI only. Defines a callback function that allows additional tasks to be done by the workers. The method R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker contains a loop, where the workers receive a message (an integer), run a function corresponding to that integer, and then wait for another message. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback allows the developer to add another function that responds to additional integer messages by calling developer-\/defined functions corresponding to those integers. R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker calls the callback function when the message number is not one of the Phreeqc\+RM message numbers. Messages are unique integer numbers. Phreeqc\+RM uses integers in a range beginning at 0. It is suggested that developers use message numbers starting at 1000 or higher for their tasks. The callback function calls a developer-\/defined function specified by the message number and then returns to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker to wait for another message. ~\newline
~\newline
 For Fortran, the functions that are called from the callback function can use U\+SE statements to find the data necessary to perform the tasks, and the only argument to the callback function is an integer message argument. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback} must be called by each worker before R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker is called. ~\newline
~\newline
 The motivation for this method is to allow the workers to perform other tasks, for instance, parallel transport calculations, within the structure of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. The callback function can be used to allow the workers to receive data, perform transport calculations, and (or) send results, without leaving the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. Alternatively, it is possible for the workers to return from R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker by a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break by root. The workers could then call subroutines to receive data, calculate transport, and send data, and then resume processing Phreeqc\+RM messages from root with another call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a3ad87e394419ba3eef2908d643685b3d}{rm\+\_\+setpartitionuzsolids}} (id, tf)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Sets the property for partitioning solids between the saturated and unsaturated parts of a partially saturated cell. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a023fad873abc6f15379735add4ea32fe}{rm\+\_\+setporosity}} (id, por)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the porosity for each reaction cell. The volume of water in a reaction cell is the product of the porosity, the saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_af0def36565ff878bca4f5a05f8451129}{rm\+\_\+setpressure}} (id, p)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the pressure for each reaction cell. Pressure effects are considered only in three of the databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a5b6b456efce1d666d8011379a0ab58d8}{rm\+\_\+setprintchemistrymask}} (id, cell\+\_\+mask)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Enable or disable detailed output for each reaction cell. Printing for a cell will occur only when the printing is enabled with R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+On and the {\itshape cell\+\_\+mask} value is 1. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a030fb4c8da13da1e45406f6f0be8af0f}{rm\+\_\+setprintchemistryon}} (id, workers, initial\+\_\+phreeqc, utility)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Setting to enable or disable printing detailed output from reaction calculations to the output file for a set of cells defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+Mask. The detailed output prints all of the output typical of a P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC reaction calculation, which includes solution descriptions and the compositions of all other reactants. The output can be several hundred lines per cell, which can lead to a very large output file (prefix.\+chem.\+txt, R\+M\+\_\+\+Open\+Files). For the worker instances, the output can be limited to a set of cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+Mask) and, in general, the amount of information printed can be limited by use of options in the P\+R\+I\+NT data block of P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC (applied by using R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+File or R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+String). Printing the detailed output for the workers is generally used only for debugging, and Phreeqc\+RM will run significantly faster when printing detailed output for the workers is disabled. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ae135697ee27c825b1e43932d203f4b89}{rm\+\_\+setrebalancebycell}} (id, method)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the load-\/balancing algorithm. Phreeqc\+RM attempts to rebalance the load of each thread or process such that each thread or process takes the same amount of time to run its part of a R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells calculation. Two algorithms are available; one uses individual times for each cell and accounts for cells that were not run because saturation was zero (default), and the other assigns an average time to all cells. The methods are similar, but limited testing indicates the default method performs better. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a604f311ff4dd47e0b55c8323672c8377}{rm\+\_\+setrebalancefraction}} (id, f)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Sets the fraction of cells that are transferred among threads or processes when rebalancing. Phreeqc\+RM attempts to rebalance the load of each thread or process such that each thread or process takes the same amount of time to run its part of a R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells calculation. The rebalancing transfers cell calculations among threads or processes to try to achieve an optimum balance. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Rebalance\+Fraction} adjusts the calculated optimum number of cell transfers by a fraction from 0 to 1.\+0 to determine the actual number of cell transfers. A value of zero eliminates load rebalancing. A value less than 1.\+0 is suggested to slow the approach to the optimum cell distribution and avoid possible oscillations when too many cells are transferred at one iteration, requiring reverse transfers at the next iteration. Default is 0.\+5. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aef0cbea7ba7955c4634e495ccafdbb87}{rm\+\_\+setrepresentativevolume}} (id, rv)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the representative volume of each reaction cell. By default the representative volume of each reaction cell is 1 liter. The volume of water in a reaction cell is determined by the procuct of the representative volume, the porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), and the saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation). The numerical method of P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC is more robust if the water volume for a reaction cell is within a couple orders of magnitude of 1.\+0. Small water volumes caused by small porosities and (or) small saturations (and (or) small representative volumes) may cause non-\/convergence of the numerical method. In these cases, a larger representative volume may help. Note that increasing the representative volume also increases the number of moles of the reactants in the reaction cell (minerals, surfaces, exchangers, and others), which are defined as moles per representative volume. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a174eb1088d6e5a2f50d2d819b757edc4}{rm\+\_\+setsaturation}} (id, sat)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the saturation of each reaction cell. Saturation is a fraction ranging from 0 to 1. The volume of water in a cell is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation ({\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation}), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). As a result of a reaction calculation, solution properties (density and volume) will change; the databases phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat have the molar volume data to calculate these changes. The methods R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solution\+Volume, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation can be used to account for these changes in the succeeding transport calculation. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume} should be called before initial conditions are defined for the reaction cells. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a8c944fff3f1cf3f2aaa825ed63ada72f}{rm\+\_\+setscreenon}} (id, tf)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set the property that controls whether messages are written to the screen. Messages include information about rebalancing during R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells, and any messages written with R\+M\+\_\+\+Screen\+Message. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aaf8d4ce6657900feb6ad581aafa9f07c}{rm\+\_\+setselectedoutputon}} (id, tf)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Setting determines whether selected-\/output results are available to be retrieved with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output. {\itshape 1} indicates that selected-\/output results will be accumulated during R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells and can be retrieved with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output; {\itshape 0} indicates that selected-\/output results will not be accumulated during R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_af657b0d31e9d09a40a429c668f7a4f02}{rm\+\_\+setspeciessaveon}} (id, save\+\_\+on)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Sets the value of the species-\/save property. This method enables use of Phreeqc\+RM with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations. By default, concentrations of aqueous species are not saved. Setting the species-\/save property to 1 allows aqueous species concentrations to be retrieved with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations, and solution compositions to be set with R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be called before calls to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_ab18195c2924f441603e7ecd1f9b63964}{rm\+\_\+setunitsexchange}} (id, option)

integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aa53b2e3006b83822b9bdbd37c67f7cee}{rm\+\_\+setunitsppassemblage}} (id, option)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set input units for pure phase assemblages (equilibrium phases). In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, equilibrium phases are defined by moles of each phase ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+P\+Passemblage} specifies how the number of moles of phases in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a35e0b41c327e3f5df228e73bc2fd5ca7}{rm\+\_\+setunitssolution}} (id, option)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Solution concentration units used by the transport model. Options are 1, mg/L; 2 mol/L; or 3, mass fraction, kg/kgs. P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC defines solutions by the number of moles of each element in the solution. ~\newline
~\newline
 To convert from mg/L to moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell, mg/L is converted to mol/L and multiplied by the solution volume, which is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). To convert from mol/L to moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell, mol/L is multiplied by the solution volume. To convert from mass fraction to moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell, kg/kgs is converted to mol/kgs, multiplied by density (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density) and multiplied by the solution volume. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aa88e3c585e128695991c98ff3b6fe28c}{rm\+\_\+setunitsssassemblage}} (id, option)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set input units for solid-\/solution assemblages. In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC, solid solutions are defined by moles of each component ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+S\+Sassemblage} specifies how the number of moles of solid-\/solution components in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_afb9852a7e4d8a41fa5b9e6fa6df15a42}{rm\+\_\+setunitssurface}} (id, option)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set input units for surfaces. In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, surfaces are defined by moles of surface sites ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Surface} specifies how the number of moles of surface sites in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a175641b24fc5ac336ef91114f134b799}{rm\+\_\+speciesconcentrations2module}} (id, species\+\_\+conc)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set solution concentrations in the reaction cells based on the vector of aqueous species concentrations ({\itshape species\+\_\+conc}). This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. The list of aqueous species is determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components and includes all aqueous species that can be made from the set of components. The method determines the total concentration of a component by summing the molarities of the individual species times the stoichiometric coefficient of the element in each species. Solution compositions in the reaction cells are updated with these component concentrations. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_a3827b6ec63d11454f8c6f47de3cfdd49}{rm\+\_\+usesolutiondensityvolume}} (id, tf)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Determines the volume and density to use when converting from the reaction-\/module concentrations to transport concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations). Two options are available to convert concentration units\+: (1) the density and solution volume calculated by P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC are used, or (2) the specified density (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density) and solution volume are defined by the product of saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). Transport models that consider density-\/dependent flow will probably use the P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+Q\+C-\/calculated density and solution volume (default), whereas transport models that assume constant-\/density flow will probably use specified values of density and solution volume. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate density and solution volume\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. Density is only used when converting to transport units of mass fraction. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
integer function \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacephreeqcrm_aaccf9017d63d8b6b8dada4e1f39b3b73}{rm\+\_\+warningmessage}} (id, warn\+\_\+str)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Print a warning message to the screen and the log file. \end{DoxyCompactList}\end{DoxyCompactItemize}


\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
Fortran Documentation for the geochemical reaction module Phreeqc\+RM. 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{}
\char`\"{}\+U\+S\+E Phreeqc\+R\+M\char`\"{} is included in Fortran source code to define the Phreeqc\+RM functions. For Windows, define the module by including the file \mbox{\hyperlink{_r_m__interface_8_f90}{R\+M\+\_\+interface.\+F90}} in your project. For Linux, configure, compile, and install the Phreeqc\+RM library and module file. You will need installed include directory (-\/I) added to the project) to reference the module file. You will need to link to the library to produce the executable for your code. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}


\doxysubsection{Function/\+Subroutine Documentation}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ae8a50594bacfaf961614749f94ce16d2}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ae8a50594bacfaf961614749f94ce16d2}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_abort@{rm\_abort}}
\index{rm\_abort@{rm\_abort}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_abort()}{rm\_abort()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+abort (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{irm\+\_\+result,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in)}]{err\+\_\+str }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Abort the program. {\itshape irm\+\_\+result} will be interpreted as an I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT value and decoded; {\itshape err\+\_\+str} will be printed; and the reaction module will be destroyed. If using M\+PI, an M\+P\+I\+\_\+\+Abort message will be sent before the reaction module is destroyed. If the {\itshape id} is an invalid instance, R\+M\+\_\+\+Abort will return a value of I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+B\+A\+D\+I\+N\+S\+T\+A\+N\+CE, otherwise the program will exit with a return code of 4. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance id returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em irm\+\_\+result} & Integer treated as an I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT return code. \\
\hline
{\em err\+\_\+str} & String to be printed as an error message. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & Program will exit before returning unless {\itshape id} is an invalid reaction module id. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}

~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Destroy, R\+M\+\_\+\+Error\+Message. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_closefiles()}{rm\_closefiles()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+closefiles (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Close the output and log files. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_afd0d3fa630c28207e4243323e04e56df}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_afd0d3fa630c28207e4243323e04e56df}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_concentrations2utility@{rm\_concentrations2utility}}
\index{rm\_concentrations2utility@{rm\_concentrations2utility}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_concentrations2utility()}{rm\_concentrations2utility()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+concentrations2utility (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in)}]{c,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{tc,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{p\+\_\+atm }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\itshape N} sets of component concentrations are converted to S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+Ns numbered 1-\/{\itshape n} in the Utility I\+Phreeqc. The solutions can be reacted and manipulated with the methods of I\+Phreeqc. If solution concentration units (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution) are per liter, one liter of solution is created in the Utility instance; if solution concentration units are mass fraction, one kilogram of solution is created in the Utility instance. The motivation for this method is the mixing of solutions in wells, where it may be necessary to calculate solution properties (pH for example) or react the mixture to form scale minerals. The code fragments below make a mixture of concentrations and then calculate the pH of the mixture. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em c} & Array of concentrations to be made S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+Ns in Utility I\+Phreeqc, array size is ({\itshape n}, {\itshape ncomps}) where {\itshape ncomps} is the number of components (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count). \\
\hline
{\em n} & The number of sets of concentrations. \\
\hline
{\em tc} & Array of temperatures to apply to the S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+Ns, in degree C. Array of size {\itshape n}. \\
\hline
{\em p\+\_\+atm} & Array of pressures to apply to the S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+Ns, in atm. Array of size n. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called only by root. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a8b7992170b1f1d5cd884a42e3197af7f}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a8b7992170b1f1d5cd884a42e3197af7f}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_create@{rm\_create}}
\index{rm\_create@{rm\_create}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_create()}{rm\_create()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+create (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{nxyz,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{nthreads }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Creates a reaction module. If the code is compiled with the preprocessor directive U\+S\+E\+\_\+\+O\+P\+E\+N\+MP, the reaction module is multithreaded. If the code is compiled with the preprocessor directive U\+S\+E\+\_\+\+M\+PI, the reaction module will use M\+PI and multiple processes. If neither preprocessor directive is used, the reaction module will be serial (unparallelized). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em nxyz} & The number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model. \\
\hline
{\em nthreads} & (or {\itshape comm}, M\+PI) When using O\+P\+E\+N\+MP, the argument ({\itshape nthreads}) is the number of worker threads to be used. If {\itshape nthreads} $<$= 0, the number of threads is set equal to the number of processors of the computer. When using M\+PI, the argument ({\itshape comm}) is the M\+PI communicator to use within the reaction module. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em Id} & of the Phreeqc\+RM instance, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Destroy. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root and workers. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a6f84c89597ef9e7c076d52aeadbbec07}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a6f84c89597ef9e7c076d52aeadbbec07}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_createmapping@{rm\_createmapping}}
\index{rm\_createmapping@{rm\_createmapping}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_createmapping()}{rm\_createmapping()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+createmapping (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{grid2chem }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Provides a mapping from grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model to reaction cells in Phreeqc\+RM. The mapping is used to eliminate inactive cells and to use symmetry to decrease the number of cells for which chemistry must be run. The array {\itshape grid2chem} of size {\itshape nxyz} (the number of grid cells, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count) must contain the set of all integers 0 $<$= {\itshape i} $<$ {\itshape count\+\_\+chemistry}, where {\itshape count\+\_\+chemistry} is a number less than or equal to {\itshape nxyz}. Inactive cells are assigned a negative integer. The mapping may be many-\/to-\/one to account for symmetry. Default is a one-\/to-\/one mapping--all user grid cells are reaction cells (equivalent to {\itshape grid2chem} values of 0,1,2,3,...,{\itshape nxyz-\/1}). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em grid2chem} & An array of integers\+: Nonnegative is a reaction cell number (0 based), negative is an inactive cell. Array of size {\itshape nxyz} (number of grid cells). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a6553114482cfbf520b545a4f67dcf716}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a6553114482cfbf520b545a4f67dcf716}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_findcomponents@{rm\_findcomponents}}
\index{rm\_findcomponents@{rm\_findcomponents}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_findcomponents()}{rm\_findcomponents()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+findcomponents (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the number of items in the list of all elements in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. Elements are those that have been defined in a solution or any other reactant (E\+Q\+U\+I\+L\+I\+B\+R\+I\+U\+M\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE, K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS, and others). The method can be called multiple times and the list that is created is cummulative. The list is the set of components that needs to be transported. By default the list includes water, excess H and excess O (the H and O not contained in water); alternatively, the list may be set to contain total H and total O (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Component\+H2O), which requires transport results to be accurate to eight or nine significant digits. If multicomponent diffusion (M\+CD) is to be modeled, there is a capability to retrieve aqueous species concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations) and to set new solution concentrations after M\+CD by using individual species concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module). To use these methods the save-\/species property needs to be turned on (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On). If the save-\/species property is on, R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components will generate a list of aqueous species (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Name), their diffusion coefficients at 25 C (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+D25), their charge (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+SpeciesZ). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em Number} & of components currently in the list, or I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT error code (see R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations, ~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+D25, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Gammas, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Molalities, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Name, ~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+SpeciesZ, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Component\+H2O. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On, R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{The R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components method also generates lists of reactants--equilibrium phases,}
exchangers, gas components, kinetic reactants, solid solution components, and surfaces. The lists are cumulative, including all reactants that were defined in the initial phreeqc instance at any time R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components was called. In addition, a list of phases is generated for which saturation indices may be calculated from the cumulative list of components. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
also R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Equilibrium\+Phases\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Equilibrium\+Phases\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Exchange\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Exchange\+Species\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Exchange\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Gas\+Components\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Gas\+Components\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Kinetic\+Reactions\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Kinetic\+Reactions\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+S\+I\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+S\+I\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solid\+Solution\+Components\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solid\+Solution\+Components\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solid\+Solution\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Surface\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Surface\+Species\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Surface\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Surface\+Type. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getbackwardmapping (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n,  }\item[{integer, dimension($\ast$), intent(in)}]{list,  }\item[{integer, intent(inout)}]{size }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getchemistrycellcount@{rm\_getchemistrycellcount}}
\index{rm\_getchemistrycellcount@{rm\_getchemistrycellcount}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getchemistrycellcount()}{rm\_getchemistrycellcount()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getchemistrycellcount (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the number of chemistry cells in the reaction module. The number of chemistry cells is defined by the set of non-\/negative integers in the mapping from user grid cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Create\+Mapping). The number of chemistry cells is less than or equal to the number of cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model.

\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getcomponent@{rm\_getcomponent}}
\index{rm\_getcomponent@{rm\_getcomponent}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getcomponent()}{rm\_getcomponent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getcomponent (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{num,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(inout)}]{comp\+\_\+name }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getcomponentcount@{rm\_getcomponentcount}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getcomponentcount()}{rm\_getcomponentcount()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getcomponentcount (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the number of components in the reaction-\/module component list. The component list is generated by calls to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components. The return value from the last call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components is equal to the return value from R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a89e51efde75f2daf0a1195029417f33c}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a89e51efde75f2daf0a1195029417f33c}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getconcentrations@{rm\_getconcentrations}}
\index{rm\_getconcentrations@{rm\_getconcentrations}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getconcentrations()}{rm\_getconcentrations()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getconcentrations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(out)}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer solution concentrations from each reaction cell to the concentration array given in the argument list ({\itshape c}). Units of concentration for {\itshape c} are defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution. For concentration units of per liter, the solution volume is used to calculate the concentrations for {\itshape c}. For mass fraction concentration units, the solution mass is used to calculate concentrations for {\itshape c}. Two options are available for the volume and mass of solution that are used in converting to transport concentrations\+: (1) the volume and mass of solution are calculated by P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC, or (2) the volume of solution is the product of saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume), and the mass of solution is volume times density as defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density. R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume determines which option is used. For option 1, the databases that have partial molar volume definitions needed to accurately calculate solution volume are phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em c} & Array to receive the concentrations. Dimension of the array is ({\itshape nxyz}, {\itshape ncomps}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells and {\itshape ncomps} is the result of R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components or R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count. Values for inactive cells are set to 1e30. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error).\\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution, R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\index{rm\_getdensity@{rm\_getdensity}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getdensity()}{rm\_getdensity()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getdensity (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(out)}]{density }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer solution densities from the reaction cells to the array given in the argument list ({\itshape density}). Densities are those calculated by the reaction module. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate density\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat.

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getexchangename (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{num,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(inout)}]{name }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Retrieves an item from the exchange name list. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Exchange\+Name. The exchange names vector is the same length as the exchange species names vector and provides the corresponding exchange site (for example, X corresponing to NaX). This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to exchangers.

Retrieves an item from the exchange species list. The list of exchange species (such as \char`\"{}\+Na\+X\char`\"{}) is derived from the list of components (R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components) and the list of all exchange names (such as \char`\"{}\+X\char`\"{}) that are included in E\+X\+C\+H\+A\+N\+GE definitions in the initial-\/phreeqc module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Exchange\+Species\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to exchangers.

\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getgascompmoles@{rm\_getgascompmoles}}
\index{rm\_getgascompmoles@{rm\_getgascompmoles}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getgascompmoles()}{rm\_getgascompmoles()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getgascompmoles (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(out), target}]{gas\+\_\+moles }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer moles of gas components from each reaction cell to the array given in the argument list ({\itshape gas\+\_\+moles}). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em gas\+\_\+moles} & Array to receive the moles of gas components for each cell. Dimension of the array is ({\itshape nxyz}, {\itshape ngas\+\_\+comps}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells and {\itshape ngas\+\_\+comps} is the result of R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Gas\+Components\+Count. If a gas component is not defined for a cell, the number of moles is set to -\/1. Values for inactive cells are set to 1e30.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error).\\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getgascompphi (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(out), target}]{gas\+\_\+phi }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer fugacity coefficients (phi) of gas components from each reaction cell to the array given in the argument list ({\itshape gas\+\_\+phi}). Fugacity of a gas component is equal to the pressure of the component times the fugacity coefficient. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em gas\+\_\+phi} & Array to receive the fugacity coefficients of gas components for each cell. Dimension of the array is ({\itshape nxyz}, {\itshape ngas\+\_\+comps}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells and {\itshape ngas\+\_\+comps} is the result of R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Gas\+Components\+Count. If a gas component is not defined for a cell, the fugacity coefficient is set to -\/1. Values for inactive cells are set to 1e30. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error).\\

\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getgridcellcount@{rm\_getgridcellcount}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getgridcellcount()}{rm\_getgridcellcount()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getgridcellcount (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model, which is defined in the call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. The mapping from grid cells to reaction cells is defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Create\+Mapping. The number of reaction cells may be less than the number of grid cells if there are inactive regions or symmetry in the model definition. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}

~\newline

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a137485f738772049a34946d7799b6ffc}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a137485f738772049a34946d7799b6ffc}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getiphreeqcid@{rm\_getiphreeqcid}}
\index{rm\_getiphreeqcid@{rm\_getiphreeqcid}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getiphreeqcid()}{rm\_getiphreeqcid()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getiphreeqcid (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns an I\+Phreeqc id for the {\itshape ith} I\+Phreeqc instance in the reaction module. For the threaded version, there are {\itshape nthreads} + 2 I\+Phreeqc instances, where {\itshape nthreads} is defined in the constructor (R\+M\+\_\+\+Create). The number of threads can be determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Thread\+Count. The first {\itshape nthreads} (0 based) instances will be the workers, the next ({\itshape nthreads}) is the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, and the next ({\itshape nthreads} + 1) is the Utility instance. Getting the I\+Phreeqc pointer for one of these instances allows the user to use any of the I\+Phreeqc methods on that instance. For M\+PI, each process has exactly three I\+Phreeqc instances, one worker (number 0), one Initial\+Phreeqc instance (number 1), and one Utility instance (number 2). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em i} & The number of the I\+Phreeqc instance to be retrieved (0 based). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+Phreeqc} & id for the {\itshape ith} I\+Phreeqc instance, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Create, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Thread\+Count. See I\+Phreeqc documentation for descriptions of I\+Phreeqc methods. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root and (or) workers. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
