\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ae04ecbc40c2459af07e1fe156adbd045}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ae04ecbc40c2459af07e1fe156adbd045}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getmpimyself@{rm\_getmpimyself}}
\index{rm\_getmpimyself@{rm\_getmpimyself}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getmpimyself()}{rm\_getmpimyself()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getmpimyself (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the M\+PI task number. For the O\+P\+E\+N\+MP version, the task number is always zero and the result of R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Tasks is one. For the M\+PI version, the root task number is zero, and all workers have a task number greater than zero. The number of tasks can be obtained with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Tasks. The number of tasks and computer hosts are determined at run time by the mpiexec command, and the number of reaction-\/module processes is defined by the communicator used in constructing the reaction modules (R\+M\+\_\+\+Create). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em The} & M\+PI task number for a process, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Tasks. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_aa8592a527010fd499050141a7f771a60}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_aa8592a527010fd499050141a7f771a60}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getmpitasks@{rm\_getmpitasks}}
\index{rm\_getmpitasks@{rm\_getmpitasks}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getmpitasks()}{rm\_getmpitasks()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getmpitasks (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the number of M\+PI processes (tasks) assigned to the reaction module. For the O\+P\+E\+N\+MP version, the number of tasks is always one (although there may be multiple threads, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Thread\+Count), and the task number returned by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself is zero. For the M\+PI version, the number of tasks and computer hosts are determined at run time by the mpiexec command. An M\+PI communicator is used in constructing reaction modules for M\+PI. The communicator may define a subset of the total number of M\+PI processes. The root task number is zero, and all workers have a task number greater than zero. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em The} & number of M\+PI processes assigned to the reaction module, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself, R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root and (or) workers. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a648f2f337ef7b2c84a6a43d18aae7ae3}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a648f2f337ef7b2c84a6a43d18aae7ae3}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getnthselectedoutputusernumber@{rm\_getnthselectedoutputusernumber}}
\index{rm\_getnthselectedoutputusernumber@{rm\_getnthselectedoutputusernumber}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getnthselectedoutputusernumber()}{rm\_getnthselectedoutputusernumber()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getnthselectedoutputusernumber (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the user number for the {\itshape nth} selected-\/output definition. Definitions are sorted by user number. Phreeqc allows multiple selected-\/output definitions, each of which is assigned a nonnegative integer identifier by the user. The number of definitions can be obtained by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Count. To cycle through all of the definitions, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Nth\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number can be used to identify the user number for each selected-\/output definition in sequence. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number is then used to select that user number for selected-\/output processing. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em n} & The sequence number of the selected-\/output definition for which the user number will be returned. Fortran, 1 based. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em The} & user number of the {\itshape nth} selected-\/output definition, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Column\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Heading, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Selected\+Output\+Row\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Current\+Selected\+Output\+User\+Number, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Selected\+Output\+On. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a9db6b89ad2b650501b612233975e22fe}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a9db6b89ad2b650501b612233975e22fe}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getsaturation@{rm\_getsaturation}}
\index{rm\_getsaturation@{rm\_getsaturation}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getsaturation()}{rm\_getsaturation()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getsaturation (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(out)}]{sat\+\_\+calc }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns a vector of saturations ({\itshape sat\+\_\+calc}) as calculated by the reaction module. Reactions will change the volume of solution in a cell. The transport code must decide whether to ignore or account for this change in solution volume due to reactions. Following reactions, the cell saturation is calculated as solution volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solution\+Volume) divided by the product of representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume) and the porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity). The cell saturation returned by {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation} may be less than or greater than the saturation set by the transport code (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and may be greater than or less than 1.\+0, even in fully saturated simulations. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate solution volume and saturation\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em sat\+\_\+calc} & Vector to receive the saturations. Dimension of the array is set to {\itshape nxyz}, where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). Values for inactive cells are set to 1e30. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error).\\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solution\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a42d09ffd37c53b22f958c168f78e746e}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a42d09ffd37c53b22f958c168f78e746e}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getsiname@{rm\_getsiname}}
\index{rm\_getsiname@{rm\_getsiname}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getsiname()}{rm\_getsiname()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getsiname (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{num,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(inout)}]{name }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Retrieves an item from the list of all phases for which saturation indices can be calculated. The list includes all phases that contain only elements included in the components in the initial-\/phreeqc module. The list assumes that all components are present to be able to calculate the entire list of S\+Is; it may be that one or more components are missing in any specific cell. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+S\+I\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to saturation indices. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em num} & The number of the saturation-\/index-\/phase name to be retrieved. Fortran, 1 based. \\
\hline
{\em name} & The saturation-\/index-\/phase name at number {\itshape num}. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+S\+I\+Count. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a837cbdc0bdd06c74bf8068a04de47fa7}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a837cbdc0bdd06c74bf8068a04de47fa7}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getsolidsolutionname@{rm\_getsolidsolutionname}}
\index{rm\_getsolidsolutionname@{rm\_getsolidsolutionname}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getsolidsolutionname()}{rm\_getsolidsolutionname()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getsolidsolutionname (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{num,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(inout)}]{name }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Retrieves an item from the solid solution names list. The list includes solid solution names included in S\+O\+L\+I\+D\+\_\+\+S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+NS definitions in the initial-\/phreeqc module. The solid solution names vector is the same length as the solid solution components vector and provides the corresponding name of solid solution containing the component. R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solid\+Solution\+Name. This method may be useful when generating selected output definitions related to solid solutions. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em num} & The number of the solid solution name to be retrieved. Fortran, 1 based. \\
\hline
{\em name} & The solid solution name at number {\itshape num}. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solid\+Solution\+Components\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solid\+Solution\+Components\+Name. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a3123208fcb13e8f7ead08fc1314d447c}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a3123208fcb13e8f7ead08fc1314d447c}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getsolutionvolume@{rm\_getsolutionvolume}}
\index{rm\_getsolutionvolume@{rm\_getsolutionvolume}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getsolutionvolume()}{rm\_getsolutionvolume()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getsolutionvolume (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(out)}]{vol }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer solution volumes from the reaction cells to the array given in the argument list ({\itshape vol}). Solution volumes are those calculated by the reaction module. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate solution volume\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em vol} & Array to receive the solution volumes. Dimension of the array is ({\itshape nxyz}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells. Values for inactive cells are set to 1e30. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_affc2fce2c476d9efb90f20ab1504ff7b}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_affc2fce2c476d9efb90f20ab1504ff7b}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getspeciesconcentrations@{rm\_getspeciesconcentrations}}
\index{rm\_getspeciesconcentrations@{rm\_getspeciesconcentrations}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getspeciesconcentrations()}{rm\_getspeciesconcentrations()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getspeciesconcentrations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(out)}]{species\+\_\+conc }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer concentrations of aqueous species to the array argument ({\itshape species\+\_\+conc}) This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. The list of aqueous species is determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components and includes all aqueous species that can be made from the set of components. Solution volumes used to calculate mol/L are calculated by the reaction module. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate solution volume\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em species\+\_\+conc} & Array to receive the aqueous species concentrations. Dimension of the array is ({\itshape nxyz}, {\itshape nspecies}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count), and {\itshape nspecies} is the number of aqueous species (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count). Concentrations are moles per liter. Values for inactive cells are set to 1e30. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+D25, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Gammas, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Molalities, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Save\+On, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+SpeciesZ, ~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On, R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getspeciesd25 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(out)}]{diffc }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfers diffusion coefficients at 25C to the array argument ({\itshape diffc}). This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. Diffusion coefficients are defined in S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+N\+\_\+\+S\+P\+E\+C\+I\+ES data blocks, normally in the database file. Databases distributed with the reaction module that have diffusion coefficients defined are phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em diffc} & Array to receive the diffusion coefficients at 25 C, m$^\wedge$2/s. Dimension of the array is {\itshape nspecies}, where {\itshape nspecies} is is the number of aqueous species (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a6c26756a858e914054cc0a901e6d42a2}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a6c26756a858e914054cc0a901e6d42a2}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getspeciessaveon@{rm\_getspeciessaveon}}
\index{rm\_getspeciessaveon@{rm\_getspeciessaveon}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getspeciessaveon()}{rm\_getspeciessaveon()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getspeciessaveon (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the value of the species-\/save property. By default, concentrations of aqueous species are not saved. Setting the species-\/save property to true allows aqueous species concentrations to be retrieved with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations, and solution compositions to be set with R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0, species are not saved; 1, species are saved; negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+D25, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Gammas, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Molalities, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+SpeciesZ, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On, R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root and (or) workers. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a412fcc30015d6930fad155ad552e3566}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a412fcc30015d6930fad155ad552e3566}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_getspeciesz@{rm\_getspeciesz}}
\index{rm\_getspeciesz@{rm\_getspeciesz}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_getspeciesz()}{rm\_getspeciesz()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+getspeciesz (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(out)}]{z }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfers the charge of each aqueous species to the array argument ({\itshape z}). This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em z} & Array that receives the charge for each aqueous species. Dimension of the array is {\itshape nspecies}, where {\itshape nspecies} is is the number of aqueous species (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count). \\

{\footnotesize\ttfamily double precision function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+gettimeconversion (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns a multiplier to convert time from seconds to another unit, as specified by the user. The reaction module uses seconds as the time unit. The user can set a conversion factor (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Time\+Conversion) and retrieve it with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Time\+Conversion. The reaction module only uses the conversion factor when printing the long version of cell chemistry (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+On), which is rare. Default conversion factor is 1.\+0.

Returns the current simulation time step in seconds. This is the time over which kinetic reactions are integrated in a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells. The reaction module does not change the time step value, so the returned value is equal to the default (0.\+0) or the last time step set by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Time\+Step.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a767950773edd97935ca81bf9a40694a8}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a767950773edd97935ca81bf9a40694a8}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_initialphreeqc2concentrations@{rm\_initialphreeqc2concentrations}}
\index{rm\_initialphreeqc2concentrations@{rm\_initialphreeqc2concentrations}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_initialphreeqc2concentrations()}{rm\_initialphreeqc2concentrations()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+initialphreeqc2concentrations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(out)}]{bc\+\_\+conc,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n\+\_\+boundary,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{bc1,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), intent(in), optional}]{bc2,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in), optional}]{f1 }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Fills an array ({\itshape bc\+\_\+conc}) with concentrations from solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. The method is used to obtain concentrations for boundary conditions. If a negative value is used for a cell in {\itshape bc1}, then the highest numbered solution in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will be used for that cell. Concentrations may be a mixture of two solutions, {\itshape bc1} and {\itshape bc2}, with a mixing fraction for {\itshape bc1} 1 of {\itshape f1} and mixing fraction for {\itshape bc2} of (1 -\/ {\itshape f1}). A negative value for {\itshape bc2} implies no mixing, and the associated value for {\itshape f1} is ignored. If {\itshape bc2} and {\itshape f1} are omitted, no mixing is used; concentrations are derived from {\itshape bc1} only. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em bc\+\_\+conc} & Array of concentrations extracted from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. The dimension of {\itshape bc\+\_\+conc} is ({\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}, {\itshape ncomp}), where {\itshape ncomp} is the number of components returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components or R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count. \\
\hline
{\em n\+\_\+boundary} & The number of boundary condition solutions that need to be filled. \\
\hline
{\em bc1} & Array of solution index numbers that refer to solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. Size is {\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}. \\
\hline
{\em bc2} & Array of solution index numbers that that refer to solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance and are defined to mix with {\itshape bc1}. Size is {\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}. Optional in Fortran. \\
\hline
{\em f1} & Fraction of {\itshape bc1} that mixes with (1-\/{\itshape f1}) of {\itshape bc2}. Size is (n\+\_\+boundary). Optional in Fortran. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
Here is the call graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{namespacephreeqcrm_a767950773edd97935ca81bf9a40694a8_cgraph}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ac3d7e7db76abda97a3d11b3ff1903322}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ac3d7e7db76abda97a3d11b3ff1903322}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_initialphreeqc2module@{rm\_initialphreeqc2module}}
\index{rm\_initialphreeqc2module@{rm\_initialphreeqc2module}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_initialphreeqc2module()}{rm\_initialphreeqc2module()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+initialphreeqc2module (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in)}]{ic1,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in), optional}]{ic2,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in), optional}]{f1 }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer solutions and reactants from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance to the reaction-\/module workers, possibly with mixing. In its simplest form, {\itshape ic1} is used to select initial conditions, including solutions and reactants, for each cell of the model, without mixing. {\itshape ic1} is dimensioned ({\itshape nxyz}, 7), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). The dimension of 7 refers to solutions and reactants in the following order\+: (1) S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+NS, (2) E\+Q\+U\+I\+L\+I\+B\+R\+I\+U\+M\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+S\+ES, (3) E\+X\+C\+H\+A\+N\+GE, (4) S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE, (5) G\+A\+S\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE, (6) S\+O\+L\+I\+D\+\_\+\+S\+O\+L\+U\+T\+I\+O\+NS, and (7) K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS. In Fortran, ic1(100, 4) = 2, indicates that cell 99 (0 based) contains the S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE definition with user number 2 that has been defined in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance (either by R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+File or R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+String). ~\newline
~\newline
 It is also possible to mix solutions and reactants to obtain the initial conditions for cells. For mixing, {\itshape ic2} contains numbers for a second entity that mixes with the entity defined in {\itshape ic1}. {\itshape F1} contains the mixing fraction for {\itshape ic1}, whereas (1 -\/ {\itshape f1}) is the mixing fraction for {\itshape ic2}. In Fortran, ic1(100, 4) = 2, initial\+\_\+conditions2(100, 4) = 3, f1(100, 4) = 0.\+25 indicates that cell 99 (0 based) contains a mixture of 0.\+25 S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE 2 and 0.\+75 S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE 3, where the surface compositions have been defined in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. If the user number in {\itshape ic2} is negative, no mixing occurs. If {\itshape ic2} and {\itshape f1} are omitted, no mixing is used, and initial conditions are derived solely from {\itshape ic1}. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em ic1} & Array of solution and reactant index numbers that refer to definitions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. Size is ({\itshape nxyz},7). The order of definitions is given above. Negative values are ignored, resulting in no definition of that entity for that cell. \\
\hline
{\em ic2} & Array of solution and reactant index numbers that refer to definitions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. Nonnegative values of {\itshape ic2} result in mixing with the entities defined in {\itshape ic1}. Negative values result in no mixing. Size is ({\itshape nxyz},7). The order of definitions is given above. Optional in Fortran; omitting results in no mixing. \\
\hline
{\em f1} & Fraction of ic1 that mixes with (1-\/{\itshape f1}) of ic2. Size is (nxyz,7). The order of definitions is given above. Optional in Fortran; omitting results in no mixing. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc\+Cell2\+Module. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a3a6b64040e8435bd9bbaa871d703a4ba}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a3a6b64040e8435bd9bbaa871d703a4ba}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations@{rm\_initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations}}
\index{rm\_initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations@{rm\_initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations()}{rm\_initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+initialphreeqc2speciesconcentrations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(out)}]{bc\+\_\+conc,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n\+\_\+boundary,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{bc1,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), intent(in), optional}]{bc2,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in), optional}]{f1 }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Fills an array ({\itshape bc\+\_\+conc}) with aqueous species concentrations from solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. The method is used to obtain aqueous species concentrations for boundary conditions. If a negative value is used for a cell in {\itshape bc1}, then the highest numbered solution in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will be used for that cell. Concentrations may be a mixture of two solutions, {\itshape bc1} and {\itshape bc2}, with a mixing fraction for {\itshape bc1} of {\itshape f1} and mixing fraction for {\itshape bc2} of (1 -\/ {\itshape f1}). A negative value for {\itshape bc2} implies no mixing, and the associated value for {\itshape f1} is ignored. If {\itshape bc2} and {\itshape f1} are omitted, no mixing is used; concentrations are derived from {\itshape bc1} only. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em bc\+\_\+conc} & Array of aqueous concentrations extracted from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. The dimension of {\itshape species\+\_\+c} is ({\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}, {\itshape nspecies}), where {\itshape nspecies} is the number of aqueous species returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count. \\
\hline
{\em n\+\_\+boundary} & The number of boundary condition solutions that need to be filled. \\
\hline
{\em bc1} & Array of solution index numbers that refer to solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. Size is {\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}. \\
\hline
{\em bc2} & Array of solution index numbers that that refer to solutions in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance and are defined to mix with {\itshape bc1}. Size is {\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}. Optional in Fortran. \\
\hline
{\em f1} & Fraction of {\itshape bc1} that mixes with (1-\/{\itshape f1}) of {\itshape bc2}. Size is {\itshape n\+\_\+boundary}. Optional in Fortran. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_aa21e0a61224e6d034dc6d08efe4f5ff1}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_aa21e0a61224e6d034dc6d08efe4f5ff1}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_initialphreeqccell2module@{rm\_initialphreeqccell2module}}
\index{rm\_initialphreeqccell2module@{rm\_initialphreeqccell2module}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_initialphreeqccell2module()}{rm\_initialphreeqccell2module()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+initialphreeqccell2module (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n\+\_\+user,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{cell\+\_\+numbers,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{n\+\_\+cell }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



A cell numbered {\itshape n\+\_\+user} in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance is selected to populate a series of cells. All reactants with the number {\itshape n\+\_\+user} are transferred along with the solution. If M\+IX {\itshape n\+\_\+user} exists, it is used for the definition of the solution. If {\itshape n\+\_\+user} is negative, {\itshape n\+\_\+user} is redefined to be the largest solution or M\+IX number in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. All reactants for each cell in the list {\itshape cell\+\_\+numbers} are removed before the cell definition is copied from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance to the workers. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em n\+\_\+user} & Cell number refers to a solution or M\+IX and associated reactants in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. A negative number indicates the largest solution or M\+IX number in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will be used. \\
\hline
{\em cell\+\_\+numbers} & A list of cell numbers in the user\textquotesingle{}s grid-\/cell numbering system that will be populated with cell {\itshape n\+\_\+user} from the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. \\
\hline
{\em n\+\_\+cell} & The number of cell numbers in the {\itshape cell\+\_\+numbers} list. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a7a638bba79ee2f1e0ee82c976507a592}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a7a638bba79ee2f1e0ee82c976507a592}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_mpiworker@{rm\_mpiworker}}
\index{rm\_mpiworker@{rm\_mpiworker}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_mpiworker()}{rm\_mpiworker()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+mpiworker (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



M\+PI only. Workers (processes with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself $>$ 0) must call R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker to be able to respond to messages from the root to accept data, perform calculations, and (or) return data. R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker contains a loop that reads a message from root, performs a task, and waits for another message from root. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations, R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations are examples of methods that send a message from root to get the workers to perform a task. The workers will respond to all methods that are designated \char`\"{}workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\char`\"{} in the M\+PI section of the method documentation. The workers will continue to respond to messages from root until root calls R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break. ~\newline
~\newline
 (Advanced) The list of tasks that the workers perform can be extended by using R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback. It is then possible to use the M\+PI processes to perform other developer-\/defined tasks, such as transport calculations, without exiting from the R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker loop. Alternatively, root calls R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break to allow the workers to continue past a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. The workers perform developer-\/defined calculations, and then R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker is called again to respond to requests from root to perform reaction-\/module tasks. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker returns a value only when R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break is called by root. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by all workers. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_af1d51a379eeed1c0911ca1dde749e561}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_af1d51a379eeed1c0911ca1dde749e561}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_mpiworkerbreak@{rm\_mpiworkerbreak}}
\index{rm\_mpiworkerbreak@{rm\_mpiworkerbreak}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_mpiworkerbreak()}{rm\_mpiworkerbreak()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+mpiworkerbreak (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



M\+PI only. This method is called by root to force workers (processes with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Mpi\+Myself $>$ 0) to return from a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker contains a loop that reads a message from root, performs a task, and waits for another message from root. The workers respond to all methods that are designated \char`\"{}workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\char`\"{} in the M\+PI section of the method documentation. The workers will continue to respond to messages from root until root calls R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a7a50c4b05647d313f1ff16a1b3df379f}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a7a50c4b05647d313f1ff16a1b3df379f}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_runcells@{rm\_runcells}}
\index{rm\_runcells@{rm\_runcells}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_runcells()}{rm\_runcells()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+runcells (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Runs a reaction step for all of the cells in the reaction module. Normally, tranport concentrations are transferred to the reaction cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations) before reaction calculations are run. The length of time over which kinetic reactions are integrated is set by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Time\+Step. Other properties that may need to be updated as a result of the transport calculations include porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), temperature (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Temperature), and pressure (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Pressure). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations, ~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Pressure, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Temperature, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Time\+Step. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a5163c6455abf6aeff6eee80098fd1718}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a5163c6455abf6aeff6eee80098fd1718}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_runfile@{rm\_runfile}}
\index{rm\_runfile@{rm\_runfile}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_runfile()}{rm\_runfile()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+runfile (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{workers,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{initial\+\_\+phreeqc,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{utility,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in)}]{chem\+\_\+name }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Run a P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input file. The first three arguments determine which I\+Phreeqc instances will run the file--the workers, the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, and (or) the Utility instance. Input files that modify the thermodynamic database should be run by all three sets of instances. Files with S\+E\+L\+E\+C\+T\+E\+D\+\_\+\+O\+U\+T\+P\+UT definitions that will be used during the time-\/stepping loop need to be run by the workers. Files that contain initial conditions or boundary conditions should be run by the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em workers} & 1, the workers will run the file; 0, the workers will not run the file. \\
\hline
{\em initial\+\_\+phreeqc} & 1, the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will run the file; 0, the Initial\+Phreeqc will not run the file. \\
\hline
{\em utility} & 1, the Utility instance will run the file; 0, the Utility instance will not run the file. \\
\hline
{\em chem\+\_\+name} & Name of the file to run. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ae564bbeb02f655cdf8f9ec36f681356c}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ae564bbeb02f655cdf8f9ec36f681356c}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_runstring@{rm\_runstring}}
\index{rm\_runstring@{rm\_runstring}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_runstring()}{rm\_runstring()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+runstring (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{workers,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{initial\+\_\+phreeqc,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{utility,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in)}]{input\+\_\+string }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Run a P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input string. The first three arguments determine which I\+Phreeqc instances will run the string--the workers, the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, and (or) the Utility instance. Input strings that modify the thermodynamic database should be run by all three sets of instances. Strings with S\+E\+L\+E\+C\+T\+E\+D\+\_\+\+O\+U\+T\+P\+UT definitions that will be used during the time-\/stepping loop need to be run by the workers. Strings that contain initial conditions or boundary conditions should be run by the Initial\+Phreeqc instance. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em workers} & 1, the workers will run the string; 0, the workers will not run the string. \\
\hline
{\em initial\+\_\+phreeqc} & 1, the Initial\+Phreeqc instance will run the string; 0, the Initial\+Phreeqc will not run the string. \\
\hline
{\em utility} & 1, the Utility instance will run the string; 0, the Utility instance will not run the string. \\
\hline
{\em input\+\_\+string} & String containing P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+File. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a73b92c2118ef8c81acb35be400e4c422}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a73b92c2118ef8c81acb35be400e4c422}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setcomponenth2o@{rm\_setcomponenth2o}}
\index{rm\_setcomponenth2o@{rm\_setcomponenth2o}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setcomponenth2o()}{rm\_setcomponenth2o()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setcomponenth2o (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{tf }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Select whether to include H2O in the component list. The concentrations of H and O must be known accurately (8 to 10 significant digits) for the numerical method of P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC to produce accurate pH and pe values. Because most of the H and O are in the water species, it may be more robust (require less accuracy in transport) to transport the excess H and O (the H and O not in water) and water. The default setting ({\itshape true}) is to include water, excess H, and excess O as components. A setting of {\itshape false} will include total H and total O as components. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Component\+H2O} must be called before R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance id returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em tf} & 0, total H and O are included in the component list; 1, excess H, excess O, and water are included in the component list. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ae8fd22c076ee041c289258d28a904fda}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ae8fd22c076ee041c289258d28a904fda}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setconcentrations@{rm\_setconcentrations}}
\index{rm\_setconcentrations@{rm\_setconcentrations}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setconcentrations()}{rm\_setconcentrations()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setconcentrations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in)}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Use the vector of concentrations ({\itshape c}) to set the moles of components in each reaction cell. The volume of water in a cell is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and reference volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). The moles of each component are determined by the volume of water and per liter concentrations. If concentration units (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution) are mass fraction, the density (as specified by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density) is used to convert from mass fraction to per mass per liter. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em c} & Array of component concentrations. Size of array is ({\itshape nxyz}, {\itshape ncomps}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count), and {\itshape ncomps} is the number of components as determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components or R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Component\+Count. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\index{rm\_setdensity@{rm\_setdensity}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setdensity()}{rm\_setdensity()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setdensity (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{density }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set the density for each reaction cell. These density values are used when converting from transported mass fraction concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Solution) to produce per liter concentrations during a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Concentrations. They are also used when converting from module concentrations to transport concentrations of mass fraction (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations), if R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume is set to {\itshape false}. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

{\em density} & Array of densities. Size of array is {\itshape nxyz}, where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). \\
\hline

{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+seterrorhandlermode (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{mode }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set the action to be taken when the reaction module encounters an error. Options are 0, return to calling program with an error return code (default); 1, throw an exception, in C++, the exception can be caught, for C and Fortran, the program will exit; or 2, attempt to exit gracefully.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a0161b707ac7c404b14cec4a12630a0c7}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a0161b707ac7c404b14cec4a12630a0c7}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setgascompmoles@{rm\_setgascompmoles}}
\index{rm\_setgascompmoles@{rm\_setgascompmoles}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setgascompmoles()}{rm\_setgascompmoles()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setgascompmoles (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in)}]{gas\+\_\+moles }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Use the array of concentrations ({\itshape gas\+\_\+moles}) to set the moles of gas components in each reaction cell. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em gas\+\_\+moles} & Array of moles of gas components. Dimensions of the vector are (nxyz, ngas\+\_\+comps), where ngas\+\_\+comps is the result of R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Gas\+Components\+Count, and {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). If the number of moles is set to a negative number, the gas component will not be defined for the G\+A\+S\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE of the reaction cell. \\
\hline

{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setgasphasevolume (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{gas\+\_\+volume }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Transfer volumes of gas phases from the array given in the argument list ({\itshape gas\+\_\+volume}) to each reaction cell. The gas-\/phase volume affects the pressures calculated for fixed-\/volume gas phases. If a gas-\/phase volume is defined with this method for a G\+A\+S\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE in a cell, the gas phase is forced to be a fixed-\/volume gas phase.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a9d84a73516473581c605807c48c711c6}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a9d84a73516473581c605807c48c711c6}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setmpiworkercallback@{rm\_setmpiworkercallback}}
\index{rm\_setmpiworkercallback@{rm\_setmpiworkercallback}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setmpiworkercallback()}{rm\_setmpiworkercallback()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setmpiworkercallback (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{}]{fcn }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



M\+PI only. Defines a callback function that allows additional tasks to be done by the workers. The method R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker contains a loop, where the workers receive a message (an integer), run a function corresponding to that integer, and then wait for another message. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback allows the developer to add another function that responds to additional integer messages by calling developer-\/defined functions corresponding to those integers. R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker calls the callback function when the message number is not one of the Phreeqc\+RM message numbers. Messages are unique integer numbers. Phreeqc\+RM uses integers in a range beginning at 0. It is suggested that developers use message numbers starting at 1000 or higher for their tasks. The callback function calls a developer-\/defined function specified by the message number and then returns to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker to wait for another message. ~\newline
~\newline
 For Fortran, the functions that are called from the callback function can use U\+SE statements to find the data necessary to perform the tasks, and the only argument to the callback function is an integer message argument. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Mpi\+Worker\+Callback} must be called by each worker before R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker is called. ~\newline
~\newline
 The motivation for this method is to allow the workers to perform other tasks, for instance, parallel transport calculations, within the structure of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. The callback function can be used to allow the workers to receive data, perform transport calculations, and (or) send results, without leaving the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. Alternatively, it is possible for the workers to return from R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker by a call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break by root. The workers could then call subroutines to receive data, calculate transport, and send data, and then resume processing Phreeqc\+RM messages from root with another call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em fcn} & A function that returns an integer and has an integer argument. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker, R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker\+Break. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by workers, before call to R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a3ad87e394419ba3eef2908d643685b3d}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a3ad87e394419ba3eef2908d643685b3d}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setpartitionuzsolids@{rm\_setpartitionuzsolids}}
\index{rm\_setpartitionuzsolids@{rm\_setpartitionuzsolids}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setpartitionuzsolids()}{rm\_setpartitionuzsolids()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setpartitionuzsolids (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{tf }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Sets the property for partitioning solids between the saturated and unsaturated parts of a partially saturated cell. 

The option is intended to be used by saturated-\/only flow codes that allow a variable water table. The value has meaning only when saturations less than 1.\+0 are encountered. The partially saturated cells may have a small water-\/to-\/rock ratio that causes reactions to proceed differently relative to fully saturated cells. By setting {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Partition\+U\+Z\+Solids} to true, the amounts of solids and gases are partioned according to the saturation. If a cell has a saturation of 0.\+5, then the water interacts with only half of the solids and gases; the other half is unreactive until the water table rises. As the saturation in a cell varies, solids and gases are transferred between the saturated and unsaturated (unreactive) reservoirs of the cell. Unsaturated-\/zone flow and transport codes will probably use the default (false), which assumes all gases and solids are reactive regardless of saturation.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em tf} & {\itshape True}, the fraction of solids and gases available for reaction is equal to the saturation; {\itshape False} (default), all solids and gases are reactive regardless of saturation. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error).\\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a030fb4c8da13da1e45406f6f0be8af0f}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a030fb4c8da13da1e45406f6f0be8af0f}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setprintchemistryon@{rm\_setprintchemistryon}}
\index{rm\_setprintchemistryon@{rm\_setprintchemistryon}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setprintchemistryon()}{rm\_setprintchemistryon()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setprintchemistryon (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{workers,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{initial\+\_\+phreeqc,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{utility }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Setting to enable or disable printing detailed output from reaction calculations to the output file for a set of cells defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+Mask. The detailed output prints all of the output typical of a P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC reaction calculation, which includes solution descriptions and the compositions of all other reactants. The output can be several hundred lines per cell, which can lead to a very large output file (prefix.\+chem.\+txt, R\+M\+\_\+\+Open\+Files). For the worker instances, the output can be limited to a set of cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+Mask) and, in general, the amount of information printed can be limited by use of options in the P\+R\+I\+NT data block of P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC (applied by using R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+File or R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+String). Printing the detailed output for the workers is generally used only for debugging, and Phreeqc\+RM will run significantly faster when printing detailed output for the workers is disabled. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em workers} & 0, disable detailed printing in the worker instances, 1, enable detailed printing in the worker instances. \\
\hline
{\em initial\+\_\+phreeqc} & 0, disable detailed printing in the Initial\+Phreeqc instance, 1, enable detailed printing in the Initial\+Phreeqc instances. \\
\hline
{\em utility} & 0, disable detailed printing in the Utility instance, 1, enable detailed printing in the Utility instance. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Print\+Chemistry\+Mask. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ae135697ee27c825b1e43932d203f4b89}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ae135697ee27c825b1e43932d203f4b89}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setrebalancebycell@{rm\_setrebalancebycell}}
\index{rm\_setrebalancebycell@{rm\_setrebalancebycell}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setrebalancebycell()}{rm\_setrebalancebycell()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setrebalancebycell (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{method }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set the load-\/balancing algorithm. Phreeqc\+RM attempts to rebalance the load of each thread or process such that each thread or process takes the same amount of time to run its part of a R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells calculation. Two algorithms are available; one uses individual times for each cell and accounts for cells that were not run because saturation was zero (default), and the other assigns an average time to all cells. The methods are similar, but limited testing indicates the default method performs better. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em method} & 0, indicates average times are used in rebalancing; 1 indicates individual cell times are used in rebalancing (default). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Rebalance\+Fraction.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a604f311ff4dd47e0b55c8323672c8377}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a604f311ff4dd47e0b55c8323672c8377}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setrebalancefraction@{rm\_setrebalancefraction}}
\index{rm\_setrebalancefraction@{rm\_setrebalancefraction}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setrebalancefraction()}{rm\_setrebalancefraction()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setrebalancefraction (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, intent(in)}]{f }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Sets the fraction of cells that are transferred among threads or processes when rebalancing. Phreeqc\+RM attempts to rebalance the load of each thread or process such that each thread or process takes the same amount of time to run its part of a R\+M\+\_\+\+Run\+Cells calculation. The rebalancing transfers cell calculations among threads or processes to try to achieve an optimum balance. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Rebalance\+Fraction} adjusts the calculated optimum number of cell transfers by a fraction from 0 to 1.\+0 to determine the actual number of cell transfers. A value of zero eliminates load rebalancing. A value less than 1.\+0 is suggested to slow the approach to the optimum cell distribution and avoid possible oscillations when too many cells are transferred at one iteration, requiring reverse transfers at the next iteration. Default is 0.\+5. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em f} & Fraction from 0.\+0 to 1.\+0. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Rebalance\+By\+Cell.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_aef0cbea7ba7955c4634e495ccafdbb87}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_aef0cbea7ba7955c4634e495ccafdbb87}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setrepresentativevolume@{rm\_setrepresentativevolume}}
\index{rm\_setrepresentativevolume@{rm\_setrepresentativevolume}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setrepresentativevolume()}{rm\_setrepresentativevolume()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setrepresentativevolume (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{rv }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set the representative volume of each reaction cell. By default the representative volume of each reaction cell is 1 liter. The volume of water in a reaction cell is determined by the procuct of the representative volume, the porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), and the saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation). The numerical method of P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC is more robust if the water volume for a reaction cell is within a couple orders of magnitude of 1.\+0. Small water volumes caused by small porosities and (or) small saturations (and (or) small representative volumes) may cause non-\/convergence of the numerical method. In these cases, a larger representative volume may help. Note that increasing the representative volume also increases the number of moles of the reactants in the reaction cell (minerals, surfaces, exchangers, and others), which are defined as moles per representative volume. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em rv} & Vector of representative volumes, in liters. Default is 1.\+0 liter. Size of array is {\itshape nxyz}, where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a174eb1088d6e5a2f50d2d819b757edc4}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a174eb1088d6e5a2f50d2d819b757edc4}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setsaturation@{rm\_setsaturation}}
\index{rm\_setsaturation@{rm\_setsaturation}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setsaturation()}{rm\_setsaturation()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setsaturation (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{sat }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set the saturation of each reaction cell. Saturation is a fraction ranging from 0 to 1. The volume of water in a cell is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation ({\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation}), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). As a result of a reaction calculation, solution properties (density and volume) will change; the databases phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat have the molar volume data to calculate these changes. The methods R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solution\+Volume, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation can be used to account for these changes in the succeeding transport calculation. {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume} should be called before initial conditions are defined for the reaction cells. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em sat} & Array of saturations, unitless. Size of array is {\itshape nxyz}, where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of grid cells in the user\textquotesingle{}s model (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Solution\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setspeciessaveon()}{rm\_setspeciessaveon()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setspeciessaveon (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{save\+\_\+on }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Sets the value of the species-\/save property. This method enables use of Phreeqc\+RM with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations. By default, concentrations of aqueous species are not saved. Setting the species-\/save property to 1 allows aqueous species concentrations to be retrieved with R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations, and solution compositions to be set with R\+M\+\_\+\+Species\+Concentrations2\+Module. R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be called before calls to R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ab18195c2924f441603e7ecd1f9b63964}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ab18195c2924f441603e7ecd1f9b63964}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setunitsexchange@{rm\_setunitsexchange}}
\index{rm\_setunitsexchange@{rm\_setunitsexchange}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setunitsexchange()}{rm\_setunitsexchange()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setunitsexchange (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Sets input units for exchangers. In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, exchangers are defined by moles of exchange sites ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Exchange} specifies how the number of moles of exchange sites in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). 

Options are 0, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of RV (default), {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+RV}, where RV is the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume); 1, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of water in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+P$\ast$\+RV}, where {\itshape P} is porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity); or 2, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of rock in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$}(1-\/P)$\ast$\+RV.

If a single E\+X\+C\+H\+A\+N\+GE definition is used for cells with different initial porosity, the three options scale quite differently. For option 0, the number of moles of exchangers will be the same regardless of porosity. For option 1, the number of moles of exchangers will be vary directly with porosity and inversely with rock volume. For option 2, the number of moles of exchangers will vary directly with rock volume and inversely with porosity.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em option} & Units option for exchangers\+: 0, 1, or 2. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc2\+Module, R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc\+Cell2\+Module, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ac2b7fa3afd81e2b5342c5ee297f7d209}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ac2b7fa3afd81e2b5342c5ee297f7d209}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setunitsgasphase@{rm\_setunitsgasphase}}
\index{rm\_setunitsgasphase@{rm\_setunitsgasphase}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setunitsgasphase()}{rm\_setunitsgasphase()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setunitsgasphase (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set input units for gas phases. In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, gas phases are defined by moles of component gases ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Gas\+Phase} specifies how the number of moles of component gases in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). 

Options are 0, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of RV (default), {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+RV}, where RV is the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume); 1, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of water in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+P$\ast$\+RV}, where {\itshape P} is porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity); or 2, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of rock in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$}(1-\/{\itshape P})$\ast$\+RV.

If a single G\+A\+S\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+SE definition is used for cells with different initial porosity, the three options scale quite differently. For option 0, the number of moles of a gas component will be the same regardless of porosity. For option 1, the number of moles of a gas component will be vary directly with porosity and inversely with rock volume. For option 2, the number of moles of a gas component will vary directly with rock volume and inversely with porosity.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em option} & Units option for gas phases\+: 0, 1, or 2. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc2\+Module, R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc\+Cell2\+Module, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
Here is the caller graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_ab20b759fec4e14f04bf607f3783f9657}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_ab20b759fec4e14f04bf607f3783f9657}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setunitskinetics@{rm\_setunitskinetics}}
\index{rm\_setunitskinetics@{rm\_setunitskinetics}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setunitskinetics()}{rm\_setunitskinetics()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setunitskinetics (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set input units for kinetic reactants. 

In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, kinetics are defined by moles of kinetic reactants ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Kinetics} specifies how the number of moles of kinetic reactants in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}).

Options are 0, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of RV (default), {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+RV}, where RV is the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume); 1, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of water in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+P$\ast$\+RV}, where {\itshape P} is porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity); or 2, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of rock in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$}(1-\/{\itshape P})$\ast$\+RV.

If a single K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS definition is used for cells with different initial porosity, the three options scale quite differently. For option 0, the number of moles of kinetic reactants will be the same regardless of porosity. For option 1, the number of moles of kinetic reactants will be vary directly with porosity and inversely with rock volume. For option 2, the number of moles of kinetic reactants will vary directly with rock volume and inversely with porosity.

Note that the volume of water in a cell in the reaction module is equal to the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), the saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume), which is usually less than 1 liter. It is important to write the R\+A\+T\+ES definitions for homogeneous (aqueous) kinetic reactions to account for the current volume of water, often by calculating the rate of reaction per liter of water and multiplying by the volume of water (Basic function S\+O\+L\+N\+\_\+\+V\+OL).

Rates that depend on surface area of solids, are not dependent on the volume of water. However, it is important to get the correct surface area for the kinetic reaction. To scale the surface area with the number of moles, the specific area (m$^\wedge$2 per mole of reactant) can be defined as a parameter (K\+I\+N\+E\+T\+I\+CS; -\/parm), which is multiplied by the number of moles of reactant (Basic function M) in R\+A\+T\+ES to obtain the surface area.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em option} & Units option for kinetic reactants\+: 0, 1, or 2. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc2\+Module, R\+M\+\_\+\+Initial\+Phreeqc\+Cell2\+Module, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{rm\_setunitsppassemblage@{rm\_setunitsppassemblage}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setunitsppassemblage()}{rm\_setunitsppassemblage()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setunitsppassemblage (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set input units for pure phase assemblages (equilibrium phases). In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, equilibrium phases are defined by moles of each phase ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+P\+Passemblage} specifies how the number of moles of phases in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). 

Options are 0, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of RV (default), {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+RV}, where RV is the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume); 1, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of water in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+P$\ast$\+RV}, where {\itshape P} is porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity); or 2, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of rock in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$}(1-\/{\itshape P})$\ast$\+RV.

If a single E\+Q\+U\+I\+L\+I\+B\+R\+I\+U\+M\+\_\+\+P\+H\+A\+S\+ES definition is used for cells with different initial porosity, the three options scale quite differently. For option 0, the number of moles of a mineral will be the same regardless of porosity. For option 1, the number of moles of a mineral will be vary directly with porosity and inversely with rock volume. For option 2, the number of moles of a mineral will vary directly with rock volume and inversely with porosity.
