\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a35e0b41c327e3f5df228e73bc2fd5ca7}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a35e0b41c327e3f5df228e73bc2fd5ca7}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_setunitssolution@{rm\_setunitssolution}}
\index{rm\_setunitssolution@{rm\_setunitssolution}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setunitssolution()}{rm\_setunitssolution()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setunitssolution (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Solution concentration units used by the transport model. Options are 1, mg/L; 2 mol/L; or 3, mass fraction, kg/kgs. P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC defines solutions by the number of moles of each element in the solution. ~\newline
~\newline
 To convert from mg/L to moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell, mg/L is converted to mol/L and multiplied by the solution volume, which is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). To convert from mol/L to moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell, mol/L is multiplied by the solution volume. To convert from mass fraction to moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell, kg/kgs is converted to mol/kgs, multiplied by density (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density) and multiplied by the solution volume. 

To convert from moles of element in the representative volume of a reaction cell to mg/L, the number of moles of an element is divided by the solution volume resulting in mol/L, and then converted to mg/L. To convert from moles of element in a cell to mol/L, the number of moles of an element is divided by the solution volume resulting in mol/L. To convert from moles of element in a cell to mass fraction, the number of moles of an element is converted to kg and divided by the total mass of the solution. Two options are available for the volume and mass of solution that are used in converting to transport concentrations\+: (1) the volume and mass of solution are calculated by P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC, or (2) the volume of solution is the product of porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume), and the mass of solution is volume times density as defined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density. Which option is used is determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em option} & Units option for solutions\+: 1, 2, or 3, default is 1, mg/L. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Use\+Solution\+Density\+Volume.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

Set input units for solid-\/solution assemblages. In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC, solid solutions are defined by moles of each component ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+S\+Sassemblage} specifies how the number of moles of solid-\/solution components in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). 

Options are 0, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of RV (default), {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+RV}, where RV is the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume); 1, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of water in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+P$\ast$\+RV}, where {\itshape P} is porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity); or 2, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of rock in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$}(1-\/{\itshape P})$\ast$\+RV.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_setunitssurface()}{rm\_setunitssurface()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+setunitssurface (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set input units for surfaces. In P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC input, surfaces are defined by moles of surface sites ({\itshape Mp}). {\itshape R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Units\+Surface} specifies how the number of moles of surface sites in a reaction cell ({\itshape Mc}) is calculated from the input value ({\itshape Mp}). 

Options are 0, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of RV (default), {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+RV}, where RV is the representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume); 1, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of water in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$\+P$\ast$\+RV}, where {\itshape P} is porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity); or 2, {\itshape Mp} is mol/L of rock in the RV, {\itshape Mc} = {\itshape Mp$\ast$}(1-\/{\itshape P})$\ast$\+RV.

If a single S\+U\+R\+F\+A\+CE definition is used for cells with different initial porosity, the three options scale quite differently. For option 0, the number of moles of surface sites will be the same regardless of porosity. For option 1, the number of moles of surface sites will be vary directly with porosity and inversely with rock volume. For option 2, the number of moles of surface sites will vary directly with rock volume and inversely with porosity.

\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_speciesconcentrations2module@{rm\_speciesconcentrations2module}}
\index{rm\_speciesconcentrations2module@{rm\_speciesconcentrations2module}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_speciesconcentrations2module()}{rm\_speciesconcentrations2module()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+speciesconcentrations2module (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{double precision, dimension(\+:,\+:), intent(in)}]{species\+\_\+conc }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set solution concentrations in the reaction cells based on the vector of aqueous species concentrations ({\itshape species\+\_\+conc}). This method is intended for use with multicomponent-\/diffusion transport calculations, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On must be set to {\itshape true}. The list of aqueous species is determined by R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components and includes all aqueous species that can be made from the set of components. The method determines the total concentration of a component by summing the molarities of the individual species times the stoichiometric coefficient of the element in each species. Solution compositions in the reaction cells are updated with these component concentrations. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em species\+\_\+conc} & Array of aqueous species concentrations. Dimension of the array is ({\itshape nxyz}, {\itshape nspecies}), where {\itshape nxyz} is the number of user grid cells (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Grid\+Cell\+Count), and {\itshape nspecies} is the number of aqueous species (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count). Concentrations are moles per liter. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyRetVals}{Return values}
{\em I\+R\+M\+\_\+\+R\+E\+S\+U\+LT} & 0 is success, negative is failure (See R\+M\+\_\+\+Decode\+Error). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyRetVals}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Find\+Components, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Concentrations, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Count, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+D25, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Gammas, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Log10\+Molalities, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Name, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Species\+Save\+On, R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+SpeciesZ, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Species\+Save\+On.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacephreeqcrm_a3827b6ec63d11454f8c6f47de3cfdd49}\label{namespacephreeqcrm_a3827b6ec63d11454f8c6f47de3cfdd49}} 
\index{phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}!rm\_usesolutiondensityvolume@{rm\_usesolutiondensityvolume}}
\index{rm\_usesolutiondensityvolume@{rm\_usesolutiondensityvolume}!phreeqcrm@{phreeqcrm}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rm\_usesolutiondensityvolume()}{rm\_usesolutiondensityvolume()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily integer function phreeqcrm\+::rm\+\_\+usesolutiondensityvolume (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{id,  }\item[{integer, intent(in)}]{tf }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Determines the volume and density to use when converting from the reaction-\/module concentrations to transport concentrations (R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations). Two options are available to convert concentration units\+: (1) the density and solution volume calculated by P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC are used, or (2) the specified density (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density) and solution volume are defined by the product of saturation (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation), porosity (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity), and representative volume (R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume). Transport models that consider density-\/dependent flow will probably use the P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+Q\+C-\/calculated density and solution volume (default), whereas transport models that assume constant-\/density flow will probably use specified values of density and solution volume. Only the following databases distributed with Phreeqc\+RM have molar volume information needed to accurately calculate density and solution volume\+: phreeqc.\+dat, Amm.\+dat, and pitzer.\+dat. Density is only used when converting to transport units of mass fraction. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em id} & The instance {\itshape id} returned from R\+M\+\_\+\+Create. \\
\hline
{\em tf} & {\itshape True} indicates that the solution density and volume as calculated by P\+H\+R\+E\+E\+QC will be used to calculate concentrations. {\itshape False} indicates that the solution density set by R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density and the volume determined by the product of R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, and R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, will be used to calculate concentrations retrieved by R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
~\newline
 R\+M\+\_\+\+Get\+Concentrations, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Density, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Porosity, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Representative\+Volume, R\+M\+\_\+\+Set\+Saturation. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Fortran Example\+:}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{M\+PI\+:}
Called by root, workers must be in the loop of R\+M\+\_\+\+Mpi\+Worker. 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
